I have written this book for you, my sons, having completed it as a part of the medical science of medicine in its entirety and having reached the goal of clarity and elucidation therein. I saw fit to complete it for you with this chapter which is a part of manual surgery.
For manual surgery is much practiced in our land and time, such that its science was nearly lost and its trace vanished. Yet only scant drawings remain in the books of the ancients, which have been obscured by hands and marred by errors and confusion such that their meanings are concealed and their usefulness is lost.
So I thought to revive it and compose this chapter upon the path of explanation, elucidation, and abbreviation, and to include illustrations of various surgical instruments and other tools needed for clarification.
The reason why there is no skilled practitioner of surgery in our time is that the profession of medicine is lengthy, and it is necessary for its practitioner to be versed in anatomy, which Galen has described. Until he stands on the benefits of the limbs, their functions, temperaments, connections, and disconnections; knowledge of bones, nerves, muscles, their numbers, exits, arteries, veins, and their locations.
And so it is said that many are doctors in name but few in deed, especially in the practice of surgery. We have touched on this briefly in the introduction to this book.
For whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have mentioned regarding anatomy will inevitably fall into errors that kill people, as I have seen many who claim to be proficient in this science without genuine knowledge or skill.
I once saw an ignorant doctor who incision a sebaceous cyst in the neck of a woman and severed some vessels in her neck, causing her to bleed profusely until she died before him.
I saw another doctor who attempted to remove a large bladder stone from a man by pushing it out through the urethra, but he ruptured the bladder in the process. The man died three days later, and I was called to remove the stone. Upon seeing its size and the patient's condition, I deemed it impossible.
I saw another physician who earned his living among some commanders of our land in medicine.
He quickly, out of ignorance, splinted the fracture on the wound with bandages and splints tightly without letting the wound breathe.
Then he released him to his desires, left him for days, and ordered him not to remove the bandage until his leg and foot swelled and neared destruction.
So I was called to him, and I quickly removed the bandage, and he found relief from his pain except that the corruption had already become severe in the member, and I could not save it.
And the corruption progressed in the limb until it perished.
I saw another physician who cauterized and burnt a cancerous growth, but he removed it after many days until his patient became severely harmed, for if the cancer is pure black, it should never be treated with iron.
Unless it is in a limb that can be entirely removed.
Therefore, my son, know that manual work is divided into two categories: one accompanied by safety and one associated with harm in most cases.
And I have warned throughout this book about the actions that involve risk and fear, so you should avoid them and reject them.
So that the ignorant may not find an excuse for speaking ill or criticism. Therefore, be cautious and careful in treating your patients with kindness and certainty.
And follow the best path leading to safety and good outcome. Avoid difficult and dangerous diseases that you cannot treat.
And keep yourselves away from what you fear may bring doubt to your religion and worldly life. It is better for you and will elevate you in this life and the hereafter according to your capacities.
As Galen said in one of his maxims, 'Do not treat evil diseases lest you be called bad physicians.'
This treatise is divided into three sections.
First Section.
The first section discusses cauterization with fire and sharp drugs, arranged from head to foot, including illustrations of instruments and kinds of cautery, and all that is needed for manual work.
The Second Chapter
In the treatment of wounds and swellings, bloodletting, cupping therapy, surgeries, extraction of arrows, and related matters, all arranged in an orderly manner with illustrations of tools.
The Third Chapter
In the treatment of dislocations, sprains, and related conditions from head to foot, arranged in an orderly manner with illustrations of tools.
The First Chapter
On Hemorrhoids
Before mentioning its treatment, it is necessary to mention the method of its benefit and harm, and in which constitution it is used.
I say that discussing the manner of benefit and harm of hemorrhoids is a long conversation, a subtle science, and a hidden secret about which many sages have spoken.
And they differed in their views on this topic, but I have summarized some of it to avoid lengthiness.
I say that hemorrhoids benefit generally for all constitutions with matter and without, but especially in two constitutions without matter: the hot constitution without matter, and the dry constitution without matter.
As for the dry constitution with matter, there was a disagreement among them. Some said that hemorrhoids are beneficial in this case, while others argued that they are not suitable because heat and dryness are contraindicated.
It is impossible for a hot and dry disease to be treated with a hot and dry remedy. But the one who says that hemorrhoids can benefit a hot and dry disease occurring in people's buttocks is correct. For whenever you add the body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you make the body cold.
And I say that he is correct, for experience has shown me this many times. But it should not be imagined that anyone can comprehend this matter except one who has practiced and been extensively trained in the treatment of hemorrhoids. And he stopped at the different constitutions of people, the conditions of diseases within them, their causes, symptoms, and duration.
And as for other constitutions, there is no fear of them, especially cold and moist diseases, for all physicians agree on their benefit from hemorrhoids without any disagreement.
Know, O sons, that cauterizing with fire is preferable to cauterizing with a burned drug because fire is a singular substance whose effect is limited to the member it burns, and it rarely harms another connected member.
And cauterizing with a burned drug may extend its effect to nearby members, and it might even cause illness in the member that is difficult to treat or perhaps kill, but fire, due to its nobility and excellence, does not do this except when it becomes excessive.
And we have found this to be true through experience gained from long practice and careful attention to the art, and by observing the facts of the matter.
And I have omitted lengthy discussion, although it would not be fitting for this book of mine to conceal from you the secret of fire and its manner of action upon bodies and its repulsion of diseases with philosophical arguments that prove beyond doubt.
Know, O sons, that they have differed about the time suitable for cauterization, and they considered the best time to be in springtime.
And I say that cauterization is suitable at all times because the harm caused by time can be counteracted by the benefit derived from cauterization. Especially when cauterization is for a necessary, severe, and urgent pain that cannot be delayed, lest worse mischief should ensue than the slight harm caused by time.
Do not think, O sons, as common people and foolish physicians do, that cauterization which cures a certain disease will never recur again, considering it to be a lasting remedy.
For cauterization is nothing but a drug that alters the temperament and dries up the humors that are the cause of pain.
Except that cauterization is preferable to drugs in its swift effectiveness, power, and severity.
And the disease may sometimes return, depending on the temperament of the patient, the nature and strength of the disease, and what is prepared in his body due to the abundance or deficiency of humors and other such causes.
O Lord, let not the disease for which cupping is employed be a mild one, and let it be in an organ that has little importance or moisture. Like treating toothache with cupping, it may happen that the pain does not return, which is preferable.
And as for the common saying that cupping is the last resort in medicine, this is true only insofar as they believe that nothing else can help after cupping has been performed.
Indeed, what is meant by 'cupping is the last resort in medicine' is that we have tried various treatments for a particular disease and they did not work, so we used cupping as our last resort and it was effective. Not according to the meaning understood by the common people and many ignorant doctors.
It was mentioned earlier that cupping with gold is preferable to cupping with iron, because of the warmth and nobility of gold's substance. They said it does not cause blisters at the site of cupping, which is not true.
For I have tried it and found that gold causes blisters in some areas but not others. Cupping with gold is better than iron, as they said, except that if you heat the cupping vessel made of gold in fire, you will not know when it reaches the desired temperature for heating gold.
Because it cools quickly, even if you increase the heat it will melt in the fire and the craftsman will be confused by that. Therefore, cupping with iron is quicker and more correct for us to use, God willing.
I have arranged this chapter on cupping into sections, starting from the head to the foot, so that the student may easily find what he wants, God willing.
Chapter One.
For cupping of the head, use one vessel.
This cupping relieves excessive dampness and coldness in the brain, which are causes of headaches, frequent colds from the head to the ears, excessive sleep, toothache, and sore throat. In summary, this cupping is beneficial for all diseases caused by coldness, such as palsy, epilepsy, shivering, and similar ailments.
Firstly, command the patient to evacuate with a purgative medicine three or four nights prior, according to what is suitable for their strength and age.
Then, command him to shave his head with the razor, then make him sit before you cross-legged, having placed his hands on his chest.
Then place the base of your little finger at the base of his nose between his eyes where your fingertip ends, mark that spot with ink.
Then heat the brass cautery [this is its image].
Reveal from the bone as much as a walnut or chickpea, then raise your hand and wait until it cools, then prepare your hand with the same cautery or another if it has cooled. Until you see from the bone what I mentioned to you, then take some salt, dissolve it in water, and soak a cotton pad in it, place it on the spot and leave it for three days.
Then apply a cotton pad soaked in oil to him and leave it until the inflammation subsides, then treat him with the four-component ointment until he recovers, if God wills.
And they said that the more a wound remains open, the better it is for pus to flow out, and the more beneficial it is.
Some mentioned that they cauterize until reaching the bone and press the cautery until some of the thick bone burns, then remove what has burnt from the bone, then treat it.
Others said it is necessary to exaggerate cautery until its effect reaches the bone strongly enough that some of the bone falls like a small ring or button, and they claimed that this relieves pressure from that spot and leaves the wound open for a long time.
Then treat until it heals, and I do not see either of these types of cautery except in some people, and leaving it to nature is better in my opinion. And peace be upon you if there is any [disagreement], for the head [is like] a fortress; when its natural connection is disrupted, it will defend itself, as we have seen in other limbs.
Especially when the patient's head is naturally weak, and the first type of cautery is safer and better in my opinion, so use it with peace and tranquility, if God wills.
Chapter Two
Also in the case of the head
If there is a persistent pain in the head that remains for many days despite using remedies such as cupping, cauterization, and medications made from aromatics or other ingredients, especially if applying the cautery treatment mentioned earlier has not been effective, then examine (the patient). If the head of the patient is strong and well-built, but he feels extreme coldness, cauterize him again with a slightly smaller cupping glass. Then apply cupping glasses to each of the four corners of his head until the skin thickens and the intended bone is exposed, as described. And apply a cupping glass to the back of his head at the spot known as the occiput, but do so gently without exposing the bone, as this will cause severe pain unlike any other cupping treatment. I will mention this cupping procedure in its proper place.
The cupping glasses used for the corners and back of the head should be softer than those used for the middle of the head, and this is their shape.
Chapter Three
On the treatment of non-chronic headaches.
If pain occurs in the temple accompanied by headache and extends to the eye, then the patient should evacuate (the humors) using diuretics for the head and apply other treatments mentioned in the chapters on diseases. If this does not help, then apply cupping to two points. Either use a sharp cautery drug or cauterize with iron.
As for cauterizing with the burning drug, take one clove of garlic, peel it, and cut off its edges on both sides. Then make an incision in the temple at the site of the pain using a wide lancet so that there is enough space under the skin to fit the clove.
Insert the garlic clove under the skin until it is completely hidden, then make a tight bandage and leave it for about fifteen hours. Then remove the garlic clove and allow the wound to heal for two or three days before dressing it.
Apply a bandage soaked in fat to draw out the wound, then treat it with ointment until it heals, if God wills. Alternatively, you can use some of the cauterizing drugs mentioned in the eighteenth chapter on cauterizing drugs.
If cauterizing with iron, this is how it should be done: Heat the brand of this shape:
And it is called the 'screw cautery' because its head has some convexity like a screw, and there is a small groove in its center.
Then place it on the painful spot, grasp your hand firmly while gently turning the iron; let the amount burned be like half the thickness of the skin. And raise your hand so as not to burn the vein underneath which would cause bleeding. Then immerse a wad in saltwater and apply it to the spot, leaving it for three days. Then change the dressing with oil until it heals, if God wills.
If you wish, cauterize this wound with the sharp tip protruding from the brand, taking care not to cut the vein in this non-chronic ulcer.
Chapter Four.
On cauterizing chronic ulcers.
If you have treated the ulcer with what has been mentioned earlier regarding cautery, and if the treatment did not succeed, and you see that the ulcer does not respond to any of the previously mentioned cauterizations by fire or medication, Then heat the sharp cautery until it turns white, having first made a mark on the painful spot about half a finger's length or more. Then grasp your hand once and pull the cautery strongly until you sever the vein and reach near to the bone.
But take care not to touch the jawbone that moves during chewing, lest you burn the muscle or its motor nerve causing spasm.
And beware of the blood from the vein you have severed, for it will gush forth. Especially for those who are ignorant and inexperienced in such matters and leave the work to others.
And the treatment of sudden bleeding from an artery will be mentioned in its proper place in this book, if God wills. If you see that the ulcer does not respond to this cauterization,
Then cauterize in the center of the forehead as we have described, and treat the wound until it heals, if God wills.
If you wish, use the curette that we mentioned in the chapter on dividing arteries with the scissor-shaped forceps; it is better and more effective than this one.
Chapter Five
Earache.
If pain occurs in the ear due to cold and it is treated with purgatives and other remedies mentioned in the section, but the pain does not subside, cauterize the point called "the Point" which has this shape.
Then cauterize around the entire ear or both ears if the pain is in both of them, using the heated forceps. Away from the base of the ear a little after marking the spot with ink, use the curette which is about ten points in each ear or approximately that size. Then treat the spots until it heals, God willing.
Chapter Six
Toothache.
The toothache that is treated with the curette is specifically of the type caused by phlegm, as mentioned in the sections on diseases.
And avoid using the curette for the type of toothache caused by hollows and nerve spasms.
If you treat this type of toothache with syrups, inhalations, and gargles without success, it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three curettes. One at the base of the ear, the second a little below the cheekbone, and the third at the junction of the lips.
Make your curette from the opposite side of the painful area, as relaxation occurs on the healthy side.
The shape of the curette should be such that one end faces the upper tip of the ear under the horn of the head slightly, and another on the cheekbone. Its length should be approximately the length of a thumb.
Insert the curette with your hand until it burns through about half the thickness of the skin. This is the shape of the forceps, which is a type of scissor-like instrument that was previously shown, but slightly finer as you can see. It is preferable for the blade to be a little thicker. Then treat the spot with what was mentioned earlier until it heals, God willing.
Chapter Seven
In case of chronic stroke.
If the stroke is chronic and has been treated with what we have mentioned, but treatment has not been effective and there is no fever, then administer four leeches. Apply one leech to each of his temples, one to the middle of his head as mentioned earlier, and one to the back of his head as stated above.
And for cauterization as described above, you may also apply a leech to the mouth of the stomach, and then treat as mentioned.
Chapter Eight.
In case of amnesia.
He who suffers from phlegm-induced amnesia should initially be given large quantities of Aragat and brain-cleansing herbs to drink.
Then, shave his entire head and apply a poultice of mustard seed paste on the back of his neck, leaving it on repeatedly as it is beneficial for this condition.
And do this for the specific nerve mentioned earlier. If he is not cured, then apply three leeches to the back of his head, arranged from the top of his head to the bottom of his neck.
And place a finger's width between each leech, then treat the leeches as mentioned. If you wish to increase the number of leeches and he can tolerate it, apply an additional leech in the middle.
If you wish to further increase the number of leeches, apply them to both temples and treat until he is cured. The cauterization should be performed using a hot iron as previously described.
Chapter Nine.
In case of paralysis and relaxation of all limbs.
It is recommended to first purify the head with Aragat and what was mentioned earlier, then shave the patient's head and apply one leech in the middle of his head, one on each temple, and one on the back of his head.
And three leeches on the nape of the neck. If you need to apply more for a case of relaxation of limbs and the patient can tolerate it, and the condition is severe, then apply four leeches on his back. And cauterize until most of the skin is burned and then raise your hand. Then treat as mentioned earlier until he is cured, if God wills it. The cauterization should be performed using a hot iron.
Chapter Ten
On Epilepsy
The treatment for a person who has epilepsy due to phlegm should first involve cleansing the brain with large leeches and other remedies mentioned in the previous section, provided the patient is adult-sized and able-bodied enough to endure such treatments.
However, if the patient is a child who cannot tolerate medications, then use the purgative and diuretic drugs for the brain many days beforehand while improving his/her diet.
Then shave his head and apply a cup on the crown of his head as described previously, then another one at the back of his neck. And place a cup on each horn of his head. If the patient is strong and able-bodied, apply the cupping glasses mentioned in the treatment for paralysis and relax the body by pressing on the nape of the neck and back vertebrae. The cups should be made of gold according to the previously described method.
But if the patient is a child, make the cups mild as shown in this figure.
Chapter Eleven
On Melancholia
If the cause of melancholy is corrupt humors and thick phlegm, apply the cupping glasses mentioned in the treatment for paralysis.
If the cause of melancholy is an inclination towards black bile and the patient's body is moist and impure, cleanse his brain according to the methods mentioned in the previous sections.
Then shave the patient's head, make a tight cap of linen like a crown, and place it on his head while he sits cross-legged holding it from all sides. Then take one ladle of old sheep's tail fat.
Heat it gently over the fire until it is moderately warm, enough to tolerate if placed on a finger. Then pour it onto the patient's head within the cap and let it cool down. Repeat this procedure once a week along with other appropriate treatments, God willing, until he recovers.
If you wish, apply small dry cupping glasses without holding them with your hand but rather allowing them to stick by themselves. This type of cupping moistens the brain moderately.
Then lay on it a linen cloth soaked in sesame oil or chicken fat.
Chapter Twelve
Regarding the watering of the eye.
If you find, at the outset, that water is flowing from the eye with the signs mentioned in the section, then hasten to treat the patient by cleansing his head and face of all moistures, and make him sweat freely in the bathhouse for a few days.
Then pass a bandage around his head, tying it in the middle of his head, and then tie two more on either side if the watering is from both eyes. If it is only one eye, tie it on that side alone.
Then cut with the scalpel all the veins and arteries that are under the skin, ensuring that the incisions are long and wide across the cheeks. Be cautious of blood loss.
If you see any among them, cut it off at its origin with whatever treatment is possible. We will come to the wisdom of tying and cutting vessels later, and we will be cautious about bleeding.
He may also make two deep incisions on either side of the nape of the neck beneath the bones.
Chapter Thirteen
Regarding chronic weeping (epiphora).
If the tears of the eye are chronic and persistent, and if it is known that this is due to veins and arteries on the surface of the head from outside the head, then tie up with the suture described at the beginning of watering of the eye. Make a bandage around the middle of the head, two on each cheek and two below the occipital bones. If more is needed, tie one on either side of the eye's tail at the corner of the eyebrow using a small scalpel.
Chapter Fourteen
Regarding tying off a running nose (epistaxis).
If, after treating him with what was mentioned in the section and it did not work, then quickly treat the patient by cauterizing three times at night. Then shave his head and tie a bandage around the middle of his head with an oily scalpel. Then tie with the cauterizing iron two ties above the eyebrows under the hair, being careful not to cut the artery. This is what the cauterizing iron looks like:
The Fifteenth Chapter
In treating drooping eyelids
If the eyelid droops due to illness or dampness, apply this ironing technique once using a crescent-shaped iron.
And if you wish, apply it twice above the eyebrows on each side, avoiding the temples; let the length of each application be equal to that of the eyebrow.
Do not press too hard with the iron, but only until a third of the skin is burnt; let the shape of the iron be as described.
The Sixteenth Chapter
In treating eyelid inflammation
If the inflammation turns inward, then cauterize the eye in two ways: Either by fire cauterization or by applying a burnt medicine; regarding fire cauterization, instruct the patient beforehand to leave their lashes alone if they usually pluck them until they grow long and even.
Then, when the lashes have grown back and become even, tie his eyes with a bandage so they do not move until they regrow. When they have regrown and become straight, place the patient's head in your lap and mark on their eyelid with ink a sign resembling an almond leaf.
Let the beginning of the mark be near the lashes, then place a cotton swab moistened in egg white or sparrow's saliva underneath the eyelid, and then heat the iron with this shape.
Then cauterize according to the shape you have marked, a little at a time many times until the skin surface burns like the entire shape of an almond leaf. A sign that your work is successful is when the eyelid becomes taut and the hair raises from the eye's flesh.
Then raise your hand and leave him for three days. After that, apply a cotton pad soaked in clarified butter until the burnt hair falls off, then treat him with ointment until he heals, God willing. If any hair returns after some time and the eyelid droops again:
Repeat the cauterization on that same spot as before. If the hair is on the lower eyelid, cauterize until it returns to its natural position without harming the eye's lashes. As for cauterizing with a burnt medicine:
Then, make a paper sheet from paper pulp, then take ordinary soap and un-extinguished lime, each weighing about a dirham or similar amount. Grind them together thoroughly and do this quickly so that it does not dry out. Then, spread the mixture onto the paper pulp sheet you made in the shape of a leaf. Place it on one or both eyelids and put a cotton ball soaked in egg white underneath the eye.
Place your index finger on top of the medication and gently press it while moving it whenever the patient feels pleasure from the medication, as they will find it pleasant like fire. Once the pleasure stops, remove the medication and wash the eye with water.
And observe, if you see that the eyelid has lifted as it does when cauterized with fire or cut, then repeat the medication on the spot where it did not take effect until your work is complete and the eye is cauterized. Then place cotton soaked in butter on it until the inflammation subsides.
Then treat it with the yellow ointment or another one until it heals. And when performing this procedure, be very careful that nothing of the medication falls into the eye, as if the eyelid droops after several days and some hair gets into the eye.
Then apply the medication to that spot where the eyelid drooped, especially as you did initially. Then treat it until it heals. This is a leaf of paper pulp.
Know that people's eyes differ in size, so adjust your cauterization accordingly. This is the correct method for those skilled in this craft.
Chapter Seventeen.
On the removal of a splinter from the eye socket.
If treating the splinter as mentioned in the sections on diseases did not work, then proceed with cauterization in this manner
Tell the patient to place their head on your lap and have a servant hold their head firmly between their hands so that it does not move or shake.
Then place a cotton ball soaked in egg white or the saliva of the medicinal leech on their eyes, then heat the cautery instrument which has this shape.
This splint is curved like the shaft of an eagle's feather from one end which is used for plastering. If you wish, it can also be open at the other end; if not, it should be closed like a reed.
Then, if it is open, you squeeze the bandages and remove the excess material. If it is not open, you open it and extract its content. Then you place a hot iron on it, being very careful that your hand does not get burned until you reach the bone.
Move your hand slightly away from the eye towards the nostril so that your hand does not make a mistake or disturb the patient, lest the iron fall on the eye's fat and damage it. If you have reached the bone in one attempt, proceed; otherwise, repeat with the iron if necessary.
Leave it for three days, then apply a lint soaked in fat and treat it with the dried ointment until it heals. If it does not heal after forty days, apply the strong corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed, as will be mentioned later in its chapter, if Allah wills.
Another method of plastering the nose is mentioned by some early authors: cut a small hole in the location of the splint, then place a thin funnel into the same hole.
Pour into it about the weight of a lead dirham melted, and hold the funnel firmly without moving, so that the molten lead does not flow into his eye. It is recommended to place a damp lint on the patient's eye, soaked in egg white or water.
If the nose is burned by the lead and cured with an amazing cure, then remove the splint and treat it accordingly. Otherwise, it may be necessary to use a nasal probe and reposition the splint into its proper place, as will be discussed later in its specific section.
Chapter Eighteen.
On the treatment of split lip.
Frequently, a tear occurs in the lip, known as 'the hair,' particularly in children. If this tear is treated with what has been mentioned in the section on splits and does not heal, then heat a small, sharp iron in this shape:
The cavity of it should be soft like a razor, then place it warm in the same incision until the wound reaches its depth, then treat it with carrot juice until it heals, if God wills.
The Nineteenth Chapter.
In the case of a nosebleed occurring in the mouth.
If a tumor appears at the root of the teeth, in the palate or at the roots of the jaws and it becomes inflamed, bursts open and begins to discharge pus, causing profuse bleeding that does not stop even with treatment, then one should heat an iron on the scale of the bleeding.
Then insert the heated iron into the bleeding hole and hold your hand until it reaches its depth, repeating this once or twice. Then treat it with the remedy mentioned until it heals, if God wills.
If the matter is cut off and healed, then no surgery is necessary. Otherwise, it must be explored and the rotted bone removed as will be mentioned later, if God wills.
The Twentieth Chapter
In the case of a loosened tooth or teeth.
If the teeth are loosened due to dampness, causing them to move despite treatment with medications that have not been effective, then place the head of the dental key into its socket and heat the iron (whose shape is shown below) after placing the funnel over the tooth.
Then insert the heated iron into it, holding it gently until you feel the heat of the fire reach the root of the tooth. Then raise your hand and repeat this process as many times as desired. Finally, fill your mouth with salt water.
Then hold it for a moment and spit it out. The loose tooth will become fixed and the relaxed gums will become firm, and the rotted dampness will dry up.
The Twenty-First Chapter
On toothache
If the toothache is caused by cold or has decay and treatment with medications has not been effective, then there are two methods of treatment: either using fat (semen) or using fire (fire).
As for toothache with fat (semen), take beef fat and heat it in an iron spoon or shell. Then take a cloth, dip it in the melted fat and place it on the painful tooth quickly, holding it until it cools down.
Then repeat it several times until the heat reaches the root of the tooth. If you wish, you can dip a wick or cloth in cold butter and place it on the painful tooth, then put the heated iron over it until the heat reaches the bottom of the tooth.
To cauterize it with fire, take a copper or iron tube and heat it until the mouth of the sick person feels hot. Then take the ironing comb that comes with the tube and place it on the same tooth while holding your hand until the comb cools down. Repeat this several times.
The pain will either disappear on the same day or on another. After cauterizing, the patient should fill their mouth with good butter and hold it for a while before spitting it out. Here is the picture of the ironing comb.
You can cauterize with either end at whatever angle you prefer, here is the picture of the tube.
Chapter Twenty-Second.
On cauterizing boils.
If the boil is caused by phlegm and cold dampness, and does not respond to drugs, then heat the hollow cautery iron whose shape is shown here with both ends open.
To make the smoke come out of the other end during cauterization, place the iron on the boil once or twice, depending on its size. If the boil is small, use a smaller iron.
Then leave it for three days, and then apply a cloth dipped in butter until the burnt part heals. Then treat it with ointment and bandages until it heals, God willing.
Chapter Twenty-Three
On cauterization for hoarseness of voice and difficulty in breathing.
If the phlegm has affected the trachea, especially if accompanied by coldness of temperament, the patient should first take expectorant drugs. Then cauterize with a hot iron at the notch of the neck at the base of the larynx in the lower position.
Be careful not to cauterize the larynx itself, and only burn a small area of skin. Then cauterize again at the junction of the neck at the end of the sternum using an iron with a shape as previously described.
Then treat him with what has been mentioned until he recovers, if God wills.
Chapter Twenty-Four.
On diseases of the lungs and coughing.
If coughing and lung disease are due to cold humors, without fever or chill, and the condition is chronic, apply two cupping glasses over the lower chest near the empty spaces under the armpits, and another one in the middle of the chest between the breasts.
And the cupping glasses should be of the shape mentioned earlier, or if you prefer, use the cupping glass called "al-Niqita" whose image has been shown earlier in the treatment of earache, using about thirty points.
Then treat him with what has been mentioned until he recovers. You can also use a three-chambered cupping glass with this design to hasten the cupping process, as you can apply it in one session to three glasses. This is the image of the cupping glass:
Chapter Twenty-Five.
On cupping for headache.
If the shoulder dislocates due to slippery humors or does not stay in place despite attempts to keep it there so that it becomes a habit and dislocates at the slightest movement, do not first reduce the jawbone. Then have the patient lie on his back or on the sound side, and lift the skin inside the armpit up towards the top with fingers of your left hand if the joint has dislocated inwards.
Then heat the two-legged cupping glass which looks like this.
Then apply the cupping glass to the skin until it reaches the other side, forming four points of suction. You can also use a three-legged glass, resulting in six points of suction with the legs on the soft tissue.
This is the image of the three-legged cupping glass:
You can also add one more leg to make eight points of suction. Then apply warm compresses with crushed onions and salt, wrap the patient in blankets, and keep him quiet without moving the limb until it heals. Dislocation upwards rarely occurs.
Apply a cupping glass over the shoulder joint once, using an incision and bleeding profusely, or use several glasses in succession. The joint will become stronger, moisture will disappear, and the patient will recover.
The Twenty-Sixth Chapter.
Regarding the stomach.
If much cold and moisture accumulate in the stomach, causing it to deviate from its usual state and frequent attacks occur, despite treating it with various methods without success, then the patient should lie on their back, extend their legs and arms, and apply cupping three times. Apply a cupping glass under the breastbone, using an earpick-sized incisions. Apply two more glasses below each hip joint, so that the cups form a triangle shape, keeping some distance between them to prevent joining if they become inflamed. The depth of the cups should be about one-third the thickness of the skin.
This much is sufficient without addition.
If you wish, apply a single large cupping glass to the center of the stomach in this manner.
The cupping glass used for this single cup should be circular, like this shape.
Alternatively, apply cupping to the stomach successively by first marking spots on it with ink at desired intervals using a pen, then applying multiple bleeding cups, and treating it with the aforementioned remedies until recovery.
The Twenty-Seventh Chapter.
Regarding cold liver cupping.
If the liver suffers from pain due to coldness and moisture or excessive wind, causing it to deviate greatly from its natural state, despite treating the patient with the previously mentioned remedies without success. The patient should lie on their back, and mark three spots with ink at this specific shape and size on the liver, below the shoulder blade where the human arm ends.
Each cup should follow after another, with each being one finger's thickness apart. The cups should be applied lengthwise along the body without pressing too hard on the cupping glass.
The cups should heat to about half the thickness of the skin, no more. The patient should stand upright on their feet; if they cannot stand, they should lie down with legs extended and arms raised. This is the shape of the cupping glass.
These cauterizations can be performed using a scissor-shaped cautery iron if you are gentle and skillful in its application, taking care not to persist too much with the cautery lest you burn all of the skin and reach the intestines, for the skin there is thin; know this.
Chapter Twenty-Eighth.
Cauterization of a liver tumor in the abdomen.
If a liver abscess appears and you want to know whether this tumor is in the liver tissue or in its capsule, know that if it is in the liver tissue, it will be difficult and painful without limit.
But if it is in the capsule of the liver, there will be severe pain, and you should know that its treatment has baffled physicians. Therefore, the patient should lie on their back, and you should mark the warm spot with ink.
Then heat the cautery iron in fire; it is the one that resembles a sickle, which looks like this: And cauterize with it once until you burn all of the skin and reach the capsule, releasing all the pus. Then treat it as you would an abscess until it heals.
And this type of cautery should not be attempted except by someone who has extensive training in the art of medicine and has performed this operation many times. Only then may one undertake such a task, and I advise leaving it to them.
Chapter Twenty-Ninth.
On cauterizing the uvula.
I have mentioned the cautery of the protruding cold uvula using the roots of frankincense in this manner: take a long, dry root of frankincense as thick as your little finger, dip it in oil, and heat it in fire. Then cauterize once between the thyroid cartilage and the larynx, two small cauteries below the Adam's apple slightly tilted towards the chin, and two large ones above the breasts between the third and fourth ribs.
And two more between the fifth and sixth ribs tilted slightly towards the back, one in the middle of the chest, another above the stomach, and three behind, one between the shoulders, and two lower down on either side of the ribcage below the cautery that is between the arms.
It is not permissible to insert your hand into the wound with a hook, but rather at the surface of the skin, you should rub it externally. Some early practitioners mentioned that some people use an iron spoon resembling a slope for this purpose.
The duration (of the procedure) is as we have mentioned for liver abscesses. In cases of intestinal obstruction with a hook, the patient either dies immediately or develops non-healing wounds at the site.
Chapter Thirty
Regarding spleen injuries.
If treating a spleen condition with the methods mentioned in this section does not succeed, then cauterize it in three ways: either with three or four evenly spaced hooks along the length of the spleen.
These hooks should resemble the shape of liver hooks and be spaced evenly apart, with a gap between each hook approximately the thickness of a finger or slightly more. The description of the cautery iron for liver hooking applies here as well. Do not insert your hand into the wound, and have the patient lying on their back.
The second method involves the elbow and entails lifting the skin opposite the spleen where the left elbow ends, with the skin lift being wide enough to span the breadth of the body so that the hooks lie along the length of the body.
Then insert the iron spoon protected deeply until it penetrates through to the other side of the skin, then remove the spoon so that there are four cautery points. If you wish, use another spoon with three tines instead.
Then treat the site of cauterization after leaving it to discharge pus for many days; this is the most effective of all the treatments mentioned.
Chapter Thirty-One
Regarding hydrocele hooking.
Hooking is beneficial particularly for acute hydrocele. If treating a hydrocele with the methods mentioned in this section does not succeed, then cauterize it with four hooks around the scrotum and one hook on the abdomen.
And another hook on the liver, one on the spleen, and two hooks behind the back between the buttocks, one facing the chest and the other facing the abdomen. The depth of the cautery should be close to the thickness of the skin, then leave the wound open to discharge pus for an extended period.
No medicine should be delayed after injury. What is necessary for treatment should be brought together quickly to hasten recovery. The iron mangle used for the back has a triangular shape as previously described, and the one used for the back is bronze.
The Second and Thirty-third Chapter.
On Injuries to the Feet and Legs.
If the swelling reaches the ankle and fills with yellow water, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot in the space between the big toe and the second toe.
And hold your hand on the mangle without twisting it, then raise your hand without returning it again, for yellow water will ooze out and the mangle will be of this shape.
Then cauterize on the legs twice on each leg, once above the knee and once below it towards the middle of the thigh. On each buttock, cauterize twice.
Leave the cautery open without treatment for a long time until yellow water oozes out, then treat it with the rest as mentioned.
The Thirty-third Chapter.
On Cauterization for Diarrhea.
If diarrhea is due to cold and dampness such that the powers of retention and digestion in the stomach and intestines are weakened, despite various treatments it has not been cured, and you see the patient is suitable for cauterization, then cauterize them with a large cautery on their stomach. As mentioned earlier, cauterize the stomach with a circular mangle and four cauteries around the navel using a thin triangular mangle. Also cauterize once on the pubic region or twice.
If you find that dampness is abundant and the patient is suitable for it, cauterize once on the pubic region and once on each armpit. You may also add two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one if necessary. This treatment is successful and will not fail to bring benefit, if Allah wills.
The Thirty-fourth Chapter.
On Cauterization for Hemorrhoids of the Anus.
If there are chronic, many or single hemorrhoids in the anus that are hard and cold, or of corrupt dampness, and they have been treated with what was mentioned earlier without success, then cauterize the patient three times below the tailbone slightly like triangles.
A plaster under the chest like two fingers, and if it is estimated that his stomach has cooled and his food is not digesting, and his face is seen to be pale, apply a large plaster on the stomach as mentioned above, and a plaster on the liver. And another with an ironing press on his forehead and leave the plaster open for some time then treat him until he recovers, if Allah wills.
Chapter Fifty-Three.
In plasters for warts.
After cutting it off, if the mole is cut, heat the cauterizer that resembles a wedge until it becomes hot. Then insert its tip into the same hole and press your hand strongly until you reach the mouth of the vein from which blood flows. Repeat this once or twice.
If the warts are many, apply each one with a plaster as described above and treat them with appropriate ointments until they heal. If cauterized with a large cotton plaster, it is more beneficial.
Chapter Sixty-Three
In plasters for haemorrhoids that are in the anus and its surroundings.
If the patient does not respond to the method and treatment described in its place and is reluctant, he may recover with a plaster. If one of the haemorrhoids becomes enlarged and pus and corrupt fluids flow from it, first measure it with a fine probe
Then determine its size with the probe. Then heat the cauterizer that resembles a wedge until it becomes hot. Insert its tip into the same haemorrhoid in a straight line along the depth of the haemorrhoid and the length that the probe entered, and apply the plaster on it until those corrupt bodies are burnt entirely once or twice or three times according to your need.
And beware of burning the nerve if there is one, or a large vein. And if the haemorrhoids extend to the bladder or rectal wall.
And beware of these places altogether, but only do this if the haemorrhoids are in a place of fat and you estimate that it is not prolapsed. Then treat the place until it heals. If the place becomes sealed and the materials stop flowing from it and remains like that for some time, know that it has healed completely.
Know that if the discharge does not cease, it may be due to a broken bone or a deep, decaying ulcer, or something similar which will be mentioned in its proper place.
The Thirty-Seventh Chapter.
About Kidney Stones
If pain occurs in the kidneys due to cold or strong wind, and sexual desire decreases, it is advisable to cauterize with irons on both sides of the affected kidney using the triangular cautery described earlier. It may also be useful to use three cauteries placed symmetrically on each kidney for better efficacy.
The Thirty-Eighth Chapter
About Cauterization of the Bladder
If weakness and relaxation occur in the bladder due to coldness and fluids such that the patient cannot control urine, cauterize with irons below the pubic area on the bladder where pubic hair begins, also cauterize on the right side of the scrotum and another on the left side.
And after cauterization from each side, cauterize according to the size of the thumb joint. Cauterize once on the lower back or twice if necessary, using the triangular cautery described earlier.
The Thirty-Ninth Chapter
About Uterine Cauterization
If coldness and fluids occur in the uterus preventing pregnancy, damaging its lining, or causing pain upon intercourse, cauterize with three irons around the vulva as described in cauterization of the bladder. And cauterize once on cotton below the back or twice if necessary using the triangular cautery.
The Fortieth Chapter
About Dislocation of the Hip
If wrong fluids enter the hip joint causing its dislocation, and the leg becomes elongated when pressed against the other, with a hollow at the site of dislocation, cauterize on the hip itself using an semicircular iron.
After drawing around the joint with ink as it rotates so that the joint itself is in the center of the circle, use the cautery depicted for the stomach if available. Otherwise, cauterize three times using a large circular iron.
Cut deep into it according to the thickness of its skin, then treat it until it heals, if Allah wills.
The Forty-First Chapter.
In the armpit sweat.
If pain occurs in the hip joint due to coldness and dampness, and treatment according to what was mentioned earlier did not prove effective, it is advisable for the patient to thin out thick humors by taking barley soup or senna pods, etc.
Then cauterize it with one of two methods: either cauterize with medications, or cauterize with fire. Cauterizing with fire has many forms; one form is to cauterize three times on the hip itself, each like this:
And make each cautery go to a suitable depth, leaving about the thickness of a finger between each cautery. Use an iron cautery. You may also cauterize once in the center on top of the hip bone itself, making it four cauteries. If you wish, you can cauterize with the circular cautery mentioned earlier for dislocated hips.
So that the circle surrounds the entire hip and burns all of its skin thickness. This is the description of cauterization for armpit sweat when the pain is confined to the hip itself and does not extend to the thigh or leg.
If it extends to the thigh and leg, cauterize twice on the thigh at the point indicated by the patient's pain. Cauterize once above the armpit, four fingers towards the lateral side a little. Use a scalpel cautery with depth equal to the thickness of the skin.
If the pain extends towards the toes of the foot, cauterize with a point cautery three or four times, or more if necessary. If it is indicated under the knee towards the leg, cauterize once there with a scalpel cautery.
And be careful in all your cauteries not to burn any large nerve or artery, as this would cause the patient harm or damage.
I have seen one and two who cauterized above the armpit excessively, causing swelling in the leg reaching up to the foot. It became blackened, ruined all of the leg, then diarrhea and death ensued. If pain is on both sides, cauterize according to this description only.
Some wise scholars have mentioned in the treatment of hip dislocation that its shape resembles a cup made of iron, with a diameter of half a cubit, and at its mouth there is a thickness resembling a date stone or slightly less. Inside this cup there is another cup, and within that, another cup.
And the distance between each of the cups is like the breadth of a thumb, and they are open on both sides, with a height of about one or two fingers. A clamp made of iron is prepared for them, which is fitted into the cups; this is its appearance.
Then it is heated in fire until it becomes red hot and emitting sparks. It is then placed on the hip socket, with the patient leaning on their healthy side, while three circular motions are made simultaneously in one go. Then it is left for three days, smeared with butter, and the wound is kept open for several days.
After that, it is treated with ointment until it heals. The author of this book says that this method of dislocation is rarely used due to its harshness and unpleasant appearance, and because few people can endure it except for those who are able to bear it.
As for dislocation by means of burning drugs, a cup resembling the collar through which the door bolt passes is made. It should be made of copper or iron.
It should be about two fingers high, with a thickness like that of a finger between them. Both the bottom and top openings should be open, and they should fit together in this manner.
Then it is placed on the hip socket while the patient lies on their healthy side, gripping their hand with a cloth. Hot water mixed with niter is poured between the two circles. The patient should endure this for an hour and a half, despite feeling a sensation like fire.
Until the sensation subsides, then remove your hand with the tool and wipe off the hot water from the hip with fresh water. Leave it for three days, applying butter until the blackness of the burn fades. Then leave it open to discharge pus, as this is most beneficial.
Then treat it with ointments until it heals. If the pain extends to the thigh or leg, make him a plaster as you would for the hip, using this sharp water which I have mentioned in my treatise on the correction of remedies.
Take equal parts of salt and un-slaked lime, grind them together and place them in a new pot which has been pierced at the bottom with a small hole according to the thickness of the spout. Then place another pot under it.
Pour fresh water over the salt and lime until they are moistened, pressing them down with your hand. Allow the pot to sit until the sharp water has collected in the lower pot, then gather all of this water together and pour it onto more fresh lime and salt.
It becomes very sharp at this point, having great use in many medical applications and for cauterizing various parts. Among the remedies used for the hip are Thapsia, bdellium resin, lime with soap, all ground together.
Galienus relates the story of an old man who was cured of hip pain and sciatica in one application, claiming that no other treatment was needed.
So much so that it is said a man entered the bathhouse carried, and exited healed. To use this remedy, take fresh green copperas. If not available, use fresh yellow coppers instead, grind them with some lard and apply to the hip where the pain is felt or in the leg or thigh.
Apply it firmly and leave for three hours or until the patient feels no more burning sensation. Then enter him into a warm bath, and when he is heated, have him enter a cold one. If the pain does not subside, repeat the application after ten days.
If Allah wills, it will heal. Know that these cauteries should not be used unless the bowels are emptied beforehand. Dioscorides mentioned that burnt goat hair is beneficial for sciatica when applied as a poultice.
The catgut should be like this: take some wool, soak it in old olive oil and place it on the deep wound that is between the thumb of the hand and the wrist, closer to the wrist. Then, take a dry sheep's sinew.
Heat it with fire until it becomes a coal, then place it on the wool and leave it until it extinguishes. Then take another one and continue doing this until the sensation reaches halfway up the arm to the shoulder and the pain subsides, with God's permission. This type of catgut is called 'burqi'.
The Forty-Second Chapter.
On the stitching of backache.
The pain in the back may occur due to many reasons such as falls, blows or excessive discharge and similar causes. The catgut is used only in this type of case.
When the discharge is cold, after the patient has excreted with lovejuice or similar substances, catgut should be sewn on his back where the pain is in three rows across the width of the handspan. Five or more sutures should be made in each row according to the physician's assessment of the patient's tolerance and strength.
The stitching is done with a fine needle, using three or four sutures per point if desired. A moderate-sized, pointed awl may also be used.
The Third Chapter.
On the initial catgut stitching of the spine.
This ailment often affects young children. The first sign in a child is difficulty breathing upon standing and movement, with a protuberance appearing at the end of the spinal vertebrae protruding above the others.
If you see this and wish to stop it, stitch with a needle that is circular in shape like this: Take the stitch on either side of the vertebra evenly. If desired, sew around the vertebra with a fine needle in two or three rows, keeping the points close together. Then treat the area until it heals as mentioned.
And beware of using catgut on the spine where there is nerve constriction,
Chapter Forty-Four
On the treatment of gout and joint pains.
If joint pains are due to cold humours collected in any part of the body, if these pains occur in the legs, physicians usually call it gout specifically.
If the cold cause of gout is treated with various methods mentioned in the section and the pain does not subside, then use cupping around both ankle joints many times, using a medium-sized earthenware cup.
If it is necessary to cauterize the face, do so with a cautery cup. If the pain ascends to the knees or other joints, which happens frequently, then apply cupping on each knee three or four times from both sides using this earthenware cup.
If more cupping is needed, apply it without deepening your hand with the cup but rather like the thickness of skin only. If the pain ascends to the buttocks or back, use what was mentioned in its chapter.
If the pain is only in the hands, cauterize around both wrists like two circles. If the pain remains in the fingers, cauterize each joint and the palm of the hand. If the pain ascends after some days to the elbows or shoulders.
Then apply cupping on both from all sides, and do not neglect good diet and taking medicine. For if one improves their food and evacuates phlegm, they will recover with this cupping, God willing.
Chapter Forty-Five
On Cupping for Abscesses
If an abscess appears in the scrotum, with some intestines and bowels prolapsing into the testis, especially if it is recent, do not order the patient to fast that day. Instead, make them use laxatives to expel feces from their gut.
Then, the patient lies on their back before you. Order them to hold themselves up until the prolapsed bowel or intestines appear, then push it back with your finger. Then mark around the abscess on the pubic bone using ink like half a circle, with its ends pointing upwards towards the body.
Then warm this iron and shape it.
Until it becomes white-hot and emits sparks, then return the vessel or container to its place. Then a servant puts his hand on the site so that the vessel does not slip out while the patient's legs are opened and a pillow is placed underneath them. Another servant ties the patient's legs.
Another one holds onto his chest and takes his hands, then the iron is brought down on the same mark while standing upright. Press it until it reaches the bone or use it again if it did not reach the bone at first.
Be cautious not to let the vessel protrude while pressing, lest you burn it and cause either death or severe injury to the patient. Know that if the iron does not reach the bone, your work will not be successful. It is preferable for children's irons to be suitable for their size, and likewise for adults.
Then treat the cauterized area with butter three days later to remove the ash, then apply other ointments until it heals. Keep the patient lying on his back for forty days until the wound scabs over.
During his treatment, make sure the patient's food is soft to prevent the iron from protruding during excretion or urination. After forty days of lying down, use a bandage tied around his waist for another forty days to reduce pain and discomfort from eating, drinking, and excessive coughing.
If this procedure is followed correctly, insha'Allah, the patient will be completely healed. I will mention the treatment of hernias by incision in its place, insha'Allah. As for the hernia that occurs elsewhere in the abdomen and was initially prolapsed, if you wish to prevent it from increasing, cauterize its opening with a round iron suitable for its size. Burn only about one-third of the skin around the hernia, then treat it as mentioned earlier. Insha'Allah, this will prevent its increase. Some early authors have mentioned cauterizing hernias with a triangular iron shaped like this.
After drawing on the hernia with ink and making two lines perpendicular to each other across it, use one smooth iron cautery at its center for the first burn. The first cauterization is easier and preferable, insha'Allah.
Chapter Sixty-Four
On Fractures
If a fracture occurs in some member due to fall or blow, and pain persists for a long time without relief from medication, then it is necessary to reduce the fracture using tongs. The reduction should be done according to the size, strength, weakness, and power of each member.
If the pain and fracture are alleviated by this reduction, then recovery from the first reduction is achieved. Otherwise, repeat the reduction process because it is common for these pains to spread to nearby members. Therefore, continue the reduction until the patient is healed.
Chapter Forty-Seven
On Treating Leprosy
As for lepers, they benefit greatly from cupping (therapeutic bleeding), especially those with leprosy caused by corruption of phlegm and black bile.
If you decide to perform cupping, especially when leprosy is in its early stages and has been treated with the previously mentioned methods without improvement, and you fear that corruption will spread throughout the body of the patient, then apply five cupping procedures on the head. One cup should be placed in the center of the head, another lower down towards the forehead where the hair ends, two cups on the temples, and one behind at the nape of the neck. Press firmly with the cupping procedure until it slightly affects the bone.
Remove the cups and scrape off the scabs to facilitate the expulsion of thick phlegm. Then perform cupping on the spleen as previously mentioned. However, if leprosy has persisted in the patient and is visibly apparent, do not perform these head cupping procedures that have been mentioned. Perform cupping on the tip of the nose, two cups on each cheek, two cups on the angles of the neck, six cups on the back, one large cup at the lower end of the spine and another above it on the same level, and two cups on the hips, one on each side. Two cups on each knee, two on the elbows, two on the shoulders, and two on the chest ribs. Perform cupping on all joints of the fingers and toes, as well as on both heels and soles of the feet.
Protect the nerve that is behind the heels lest you burn them, for it also branches to the pubic bone, another to the mouth of the stomach, and another to the liver. Know that the more you preserve this branch, the better and more beneficial it will be.
Know that the sick person does not feel pain in the branch as the healthy one does, because his body is numbed. Therefore, the splints should be made of large and small sizes according to the members and joints mentioned earlier.
Then treat the branch with powdered frankincense mixed with honey and other treatments until it heals, if Allah wills.
Chapter Forty-Eight.
In the case of numbness of a member, if medication and ointments were applied without success, then bandage the numb member with splints according to its size. Make sure that the splint is slightly thicker than the skin.
Then treat it with ointment until it heals, and for some numbness that affects the hand or foot in the spine near where the nerve that moves that member exits.
And this should only be done by someone who is knowledgeable in anatomy and the exits of the moving nerves of the body.
Chapter Forty-Nine.
On bandaging for leprosy.
If leprosy has progressed and no medical remedy has been effective, then bandage it with a splint of moderate thickness according to the thickness of the skin until the whiteness disappears and its color changes.
Then treat it with ground lentils mixed with virgin honey and the juice of the mullein plant, pigeon blood or hedgehog blood, one part each. Mix all together and apply on a cloth to the affected area until it heals.
Chapter Fifty.
On bandaging for cancer.
If the cancer is newly begun and you wish to stop it, bandage it with a circular splint around it like a ring. Some wise men have mentioned that a strong splint should be placed in its center, but I do not recommend that because I expect it to become gangrenous, as I have seen happen many times.
It is correct to stitch around it with a circle as mentioned earlier, or with many sutures.
Chapter Fifty-One
In the treatment of dropsy
If dropsy occurs in one leg and its resolution is delayed, either due to the excessive fluid or because of the patient's advanced age with diminished blood flow, or due to the time elapsed, and you wish to expedite its resolution, stitch around it with many small sutures closely spaced.
Then leave it; it will speed up the resolution of the dropsy. If you wish to cauterize, use the cautery that has this shape.
And apply it in the center of the dropsy until it penetrates the skin, with the cautery being below the level of the skin to facilitate the discharge of pus. Then treat it as necessary until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-Two
On the treatment of ulcers
Ulcers are corruption that spread in the flesh, eating it away like fire consumes dry wood. If you find an ulcer in a location suitable for cautery by fire, prepare many small and large iron cauteries according to what is appropriate for that spot where the ulcer is located.
Then cauterize around it on all sides until the corruption is entirely removed, leaving no trace of it. Leave it for three days, then apply powdered sulfur mixed with oil to the cauterized areas to remove all scabs and remaining corruption.
Then treat it with flesh-generating ointments. If after three days you find that the flesh is growing back correctly without corruption, otherwise repeat the cautery on any remaining corrupted areas. The ulcer can also be treated with caustic drugs.
This serves as an alternative to fire and is quicker in its benefit. I have mentioned the treatment of ulcers using caustic drugs in the relevant section; you may refer to that when necessary.
Chapter Fifty-Three
On the cautery of ingrown and non-ingrown nails
This condition often occurs at the bases of the feet and is very painful for the patient. The treatment can be either cautery by fire or cautery by caustic water.
For heating with fire, take a hollow iron mold resembling the feathers of an eagle, shaped according to the size of the screw on all sides and thin at the edges. Heat it over the fire until it is very hot, then place it around the screw while turning your hand around the screw until the mold reaches the depth of the screw.
And leave it for three days until it produces pus, then dress it with powdered common salt bread and leave it overnight. If it detaches from its roots, treat the wound site with the ointment that brings forth flesh until it heals, if the screws are not reversed.
Frequently, inflammation occurs on the surface of the body, especially in hands and feet. Thus, it is necessary to take a tube made of copper or iron or eagle feathers, place it over the screw or boil, then pour a small amount of strong vinegar into the tube.
And hold your hand while turning it slightly with a wink, so that the edge of the tube affects the root of the screw and the strong vinegar finds its way into the depth of the screw. The patient should endure for a short moment the sting of the strong vinegar.
Then leave it alone, for the screw will detach at its roots. Do this one by one until all of them in the body are removed, then treat their sites with flesh-generating ointments after they have detached.
Chapter Forty-Five
On cautery with a hot iron.
If someone has a chill or fever of half a day or more, cauterize them four or five times on the back vertebrae, once between each vertebra, and once on the chest. And cauterize his abdomen with an oily iron mold, for chilliness will subside and the cold disease will mature quickly.
Chapter Fifty-Five
On cautery of a boil on the body.
When painful boils appear on the body due to cold, thick, and corrupted materials, it is necessary at their first appearance to cauterize the head of each boil with a gentle burn using a wooden stick ignited at its tip by fire or using an iron mold heated over long pepper roots or an eyeglass mold.
Initially, the blood vessels may bleed profusely in this manner; however, the effective cure will not increase nor dissipate until after the patient has been drained of excess fluid through bloodletting.
The Fifty-Sixth Chapter.
Regarding bleeding that occurs during the cutting of an artery.
It often happens that a cut or wound exposes an artery externally, or during the excision of a tumor or other similar procedures, causing bleeding which makes it difficult to ligate.
If such a thing happens, quickly place your index finger on the mouth of the artery and press it gently until bleeding stops beneath your finger. Then, heat several small and large copper forceps in fire until they become very hot.
Then, take one of the heated forceps, either small or large depending on the wound and the location where the artery has opened, and apply it to the same vessel immediately after removing your finger quickly. Hold the forceps until bleeding stops.
But if bleeding resumes when you lift your finger from the mouth of the artery and the forceps cools down, quickly take another heated forceps from those prepared in the fire and continue doing so until bleeding stops.
And beware not to burn the nerve that may be present there. Know that it is impossible to ligate an artery from which blood is flowing, especially if it is a large one, except by cauterization as mentioned earlier or by excising it if it has not been already cut. For if the artery is ligated, its ends will retract and bleeding will stop. Otherwise, it should be tied tightly with sutures or medications that can cause blood coagulation and constriction of the vessel using bandages.
However, attempting to ligate the artery with a tie or by compression using cloths or application of hot substances and similar methods does not usually result in complete cessation of bleeding. If such a situation occurs and neither a doctor nor any medication is available, then quickly place your index finger on the mouth of the wound as described earlier.
It is necessary to tightly bind it until the bleeding stops, and then remove the bandage along with the wound and artery. Do not remove it with cold water alone; rather, use very cold water continuously until the blood congeals and hardens, causing the flow to stop. Meanwhile, check what remedies or medication are needed.
The Second Chapter.
In regards to incisions, cauterizations, surgeries, and similar procedures.
Al-Halal has already mentioned in the first chapter all diseases treatable by cautery and burning medications, their causes, reasons, tools, and instruments.
I will follow the same method in this chapter to make it easier for the student to understand his requirements..
Before I begin, you should know that this chapter is more difficult than the first one on cautery.
And therefore, the warning in this chapter must be greater, for the work involved is extensive and there is often much bleeding, which is essential for life, when opening an artery or performing a surgical procedure to remove a tumor, boil, abscess, or stone, or extracting an arrowhead, and similar procedures, all of which carry great danger and fear, and many of which result in death.
I advise you to beware of anything doubtful, for there are different types of people in this profession with various ailments. Some may have become weary of their illness and wish for death.
There are those who complain bitterly and have long suffered from their illness, but whose condition does not necessarily indicate death. Some may offer you money in the hope of recovering their health, but do not accept it, for their ailment is often fatal.
And let your caution be greater than your desire and eagerness. Do not proceed with any treatment until you are certain of its outcome, and always begin by explaining to your patient the nature of the treatment and warning them of any potential risks.
For in doing so, you will gain praise and fame, and may Allah guide you, O my sons, to the right path and grant you success. Indeed, success is in His hands alone; there is no god but Him.
I have arranged this chapter in sections following what has preceded in the book on fracture of the leg and foot, so that your desired request may be facilitated, if God wills.
The First Chapter.
Regarding the treatment of water (hydrocephalus) that collects in the heads of children.
This condition often occurs at birth among infants if the midwife presses the infant's head roughly, and it may also occur due to a hidden cause that is unknown.
I have not seen this condition in anyone other than infants, and all those I have seen it in quickly died. Therefore, I considered leaving it untreated. I have also seen an infant whose head became filled with water to the extent that its head grew larger every day. Until the child could no longer sit up due to the size of his head and the increase in fluid, until he died.
This fluid collects either between the skin and the bone, or beneath the bone on the diaphragm. The procedure for this is: if the fluid has collected between the skin and the bone and the swelling is small, then make a single transverse incision of about two fingerbreadths in length in the middle of the head to allow the fluid to flow out.
If the fluid is greater and the swelling is larger, then make two intersecting incisions as shown here:
If the fluid is beneath the bone and its sign is that the sutures of the head are open on all sides, and the water flows downwards when pressed with the hand. In this case, do not make an incision in the middle of the head but rather make three incisions as shown here:
After making the incisions, all the fluid will come out. Then close the incisions with bandages and dressings. Leave it open from above using wine and oil for five days. Then release the bandage and treat the wound with stitching and ointments. Do not leave the head tightly wrapped, but rather feed the patient dry, non-moist food.
Until the member (head) becomes strong and heals. Another method of incision is to look for where the bone of the swelling appears and where the water collects, as it may be more in the back or front, right or left.
By the opening, it is meant where the tumor has appeared and the watery fluid has filled. You should incise it as much as you can while being cautious not to cut a vein causing bleeding that could lead to death of the patient due to this bleeding along with the discharge of moisture.
The Second Chapter
Sectioning of the two arteries behind the ears known as the 'Hassisin'
When severe attacks occur suddenly in the eyes or chest, and persist without improvement from medicinal treatment, then inform (the patient) that the remedy for this is to cut these two arteries.
It is necessary, when you wish to cut them (the arteries), to shave the head of the patient with a razor then rub the area with a coarse cloth so that the artery appears. Then bind the neck of the patient tightly with his garment and look for where the pulse beats and the two places that are hidden behind the ears, which in some people may be somewhat concealed.
Then trace upon them with ink and cut them with a sharp scalpel until the bone is reached. This can be done by exposing the head, or if you wish, insert the scalpel underneath the artery and bring it out on top in one continuous cut, about the length of two folded fingers.
When the artery is cut, blood will flow pulsatingly, dripping onto a cloth continuously. If the artery does not become apparent to touch, then measure three fingers' breadth from the ear, trace with ink and cut to the bone. What is intended is.
Send seven bandages at once to the wound, and perhaps more or fewer depending on how much blood is flowing, according to the strength of the patient and the fullness of his arteries. Then examine the wound, if there is any peritoneum remaining on the bone, cut it off.
Lest a hot tumor appear, then bind the wound with a strip of linen cloth and treat it with ointments until it heals.
The Third Chapter.
Concerning the sectioning of the arteries in the temples.
If a person suffers from chronic migraine, sudden acute attacks due to hot and humid fluxes in the muscles of the temples or severe chronic headache and similar ailments, and has been treated with various medicinal remedies without improvement, we have tried in these diseases to section the arteries of the temples or their branches as described.
The operation on the temple involves shaving the hair from where the pulse can be felt, and aiming for the visible artery in the temple. One can determine it by its pulsation; hardly anyone lacks this except a rare individual.
If the pulse is not felt due to extreme cold, then let the patient tie his garment around his neck to warm it up. Then, you should rub the area with a cloth or apply hot water compress until the artery becomes clearly visible. Then take the lancet that has this shape: Then gently cut the skin with it until you reach the artery. Then, insert tweezers and pull it outwards so that it comes out of the skin, freeing it from any surrounding fatty tissue on all sides. If the artery is thin, then grasp it with the tip of the tweezers. Then cut off a section of it according to how far apart its ends are and how much it contracts, without causing bleeding. For blood will not flow unless it is severed completely. Then express the blood from both ends into three vessels.
If the artery is very large, then tie it with a strong double thread in two places. Let the thread be either of sinew or tendon to prevent putrefaction from setting in before the wound heals and causing bleeding.
Then cut off the remaining portion between the ties. You can do this immediately or later, as you wish. If you prefer, you may cauterize it with a hot iron to burn its ends, which serves the same purpose or even better.
Except if the patient has a fever or is prone to moodiness, for cauterization helps to dry up humidities. After tying off the arteries, pack the wound with boiled cotton and apply proper dressings. After healing, treat it with drying medications and massage until it heals, God willing.
If bleeding occurs from the artery during your procedure, promptly cauterize it with heat or pack the area with salt and press with your hand until the bleeding stops. If this is not sufficient, then insert your finger into the wound to block the flow of blood.
The wound should be soaked in very cold water until the inflammation subsides, and the artery should then be ligated with ease. It is simpler and easier to cauterize the vein using this tweezers after marking the locations with ink.
And heat it very well until it reaches the bone and the vein is severed at both ends so that its two parts do not join together, for this is an image of the tweezers.
The blades of the tweezers are like two small points, but they are much blunter than a knife, for if they were as sharp as a knife they would cool down quickly and the flesh would not be severed quickly. Therefore, there should be some bluntness in them to retain heat.
And cut the flesh quickly, for this is the best and easiest work. Let there be between the blades a thickness equal to that of a finger.
Chapter Four.
On treating continuous hot tearing of the eyes.
If the tears are continuous and their flow is from the vessels on the forehead outside the head without any benefit from medical treatment with drugs, and you find that the patient's face has become pale. If he feels a crawling sensation on his forehead like that of ants, and his eyes are sunken with wet rims whose corners have become inflamed and whose edges have become reddened from the abundance of tears, so that some have resorted to this procedure in treating it, which they call 'sword treatment,' namely ordering the patient to shave the hair on his forehead.
